< Text>
This was our first visit here...another Vietnamese restaurant recently opened.  The place is smaller than what one sees on their site ... seating for 49.  There's plenty of pictures already posted so we won't add any.

We tried the Chicken Hu Tieu specialty of the day which was good.  My only complaint is that it came with pieces of fried pork rind which we don't eat.  After removing the rinds, the soup was very tasty.  It came with with side of bean sprout & pickle.

The other dish we tried was Mi Ba Ngoai which translates as Grandma's Dry Noodles.  It again came with fried pork rind which we removed.  This dish is served with side bowl of soup which I ended up adding it all to the noodles which had a generous portion of roast pork, garlic, onions, shredded lettuce.  Another very good dish.  Both servings are a good size.
Service was prompt and friendly.
Drinks were expensive in my opinion.  Fresh squeezed orange juice and mung bean pandan milk were both $3.95 but they were in a small plastic cup filled with ice so very little amount of drink ... 3  gulps from the straw and it's all gone ... thus the 4 stars.
We'll be back for the food nut not the drinks.
If you check-in into Yelp, you get a free drink.</Text>

ZERO STARS. Very upset. When I purchased my first Bhang cartridge and battery here I was told the battery has a lifetime warranty and to bring it back any time it breaks for a new one. Also that the cartridges have been known to leak and if that happens to bring it back for a new one. After my 4th or 5th cartridge purchase a little over a week ago I noticed it wasn't working as well as normal. I expected it was the battery and brought it back. They won't let me return it without the charger. Very stupid, but fine. Today I bring the charger, battery, and cartridge back to find out what is wrong. The guy behind the counter deduces it is the cartridge, but because I've used about 75% of it, they can't give me a new one. Okay. Fine. Can you at least give me a discount on another one? No. The boss says no. And the 'boss' won't come out. Bad business sense AND spinelessness. Needless to say I'm never going back here again. I would have been happy with 10% off my almost $90 purchase, which they offer to every 1st time customer.</review>

< review>
Every time I leave the zoo, I wonder about the playground across the street and remind myself to go there. this week we finally did. Dwight Murphy Fields have a park alongside the baseball and soccer fields. It has 2 structures: one for 2-5 year olds and one for 5-12 year olds plus a climbing structure and 4 swings (2 toddler). In the mid-morning, there were some shady spots. This park is located on Ni√±os Dr across from the zoo.

Pros
The structures provide play areas for a wide range of kids.
There are bathrooms close by.
It is located close to the beach & zoo.
There is a fence between the road and the play structure.

Cons
Parking is limited (especially if there were games or a busy zoo day).</review>

< userid>
110795852624419752919<//userid>
< username>
Rok Ru≈æiƒç< /username>
<date>1496527806195< /date><Rating>5<//Rating>< text>
VAM is a splendid example of innovative fast food coupled with a fast food/takeaway style of restaurant. They make familiar sounding  dishes with a Thai twist. In particular a burrito made with Korean BBQ meat, fried rice and a splendid veggie sauce for juiciness is a specialty served only at this place. Every time I come to Palo Alto a visit to VAM for Palo Alto burrito is a given at least once, bit I try to make it there as many times as possible.

The manager of VAM is a wonderful dude named Zen and he is the kind of guy who inspires confidence in me regarding his care for food quality and customer satisfaction. He is doing a great job.

The only drawback of VAM's menu is the fact that food and drinks on the menu are not familiar to anyone but restaurant staff, so a new customer is going to have a very vague idea about what they are ordering. Ordering unfamiliar food and drinks there is always a bit of a gamble.

One time I asked the cashier to give me a refreshing non-alcoholic drink of her choice, and she asked me if special Thai iced tea would be ok, and I said yes. What she gave me was a sweet milky puss full of some berries she called "bobbins" and the drink was horrendous. This was the only time I was really disappointed in what I was served at VAM. If Zen was there at the time, he would had made sure I wasn't disappointed.

For anyone looking for new taste combinations, for all adventurous eaters, for all those willing to take a risk with their order, VAM is the place to go. There is a risk when you order something you have never eaten before at VAM, sometimes their fusion cuisine just isn't compatible with people's expectations, but there is also great reward, my burrito experience at VAM is a great example.

The only real improvement VAM needs is better interior design. The place looks quite shabby.

I highly recommend VAM to anyone, who is looking to explore beyond their usual diet. And when you go there, make sure you get acquainted with Zen, because he is going to guide you through your culinary experience at VAM.

Warning: sometimes dishes at VAM can be unexpectedly sweet. Consult with Zen before ordering, if you don't like sweet food.<//text>

< text>
We spent hours looking for somewhere to get covid tests to meet travel requirements for the UK. Not only was there no support from our airline or Kaiser, but there was confusing and non-specific information from the British government about which tests and at what sensitivity.

Google searches turned up places that quoted $200, $300 and even $400 - per one-hour PCR test - which for the four of US, with three lots of UK testing once we arrived was approaching the cost of the flights themselves. < Text>
I had a little difficulty finding the clinic.  Although the address is on Clay Street, the actual entrance is on 14th.  It is downtown ( across from both City Hall and federal buildings), but I easily found parking. Probably a better idea to take Bart or public transit. The staff were pleasant and helpful, but for some reason their credit card reader was sending out the wrong IRS code, so I couldn't use my medical flex spending account for my copay charge. Fortunately, it did take my debit card.
I was there to meet with the Doctor as she was referred by my current physician who is retiring. Dr Salmon was very personable & professional. Took my vitals, listened to my concerns & offered relevant and helpful suggestions. I would really like to continue to see her, although the location of the clinic is really inconvenient for me.  If you live nearby,
have access to public transit ,or don't
mind dealing with downtown Oakland traffic, I do recommend this clinic< /Text>
